	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Eunice Kennedy Shriver</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>Eunice Mary Kennedy Shriver</b>, <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St._Gregory_the_Great" title="Order of St. Gregory the Great">DSG</a> (July 10, 1921 – August 11, 2009) was an American philanthropist<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">Kennedy family</a>. Shriver is known as the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a>, a sports organization for persons with physical and intellectual disabilities. For her efforts on behalf of the disabled, Shriver was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> in 1984.
</p><p>Shriver was a sister of U.S. President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, U.S. Senators <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a>, and U.S. Ambassador to Ireland <a href="/wiki/Jean_Kennedy_Smith" title="Jean Kennedy Smith">Jean Kennedy Smith</a>. She was the wife of <a href="/wiki/Sargent_Shriver" title="Sargent Shriver">Sargent Shriver</a>, who was the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_France" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Ambassador to France">United States Ambassador to France</a> and was the <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern_1972_presidential_campaign" title="George McGovern 1972 presidential campaign">Democratic nominee</a> for Vice President of the United States in <a href="/wiki/1972_United_States_presidential_election" title="1972 United States presidential election">1972</a>.
</p>

<h2><span id="Early_life.2C_education.2C_and_early_career"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life,_education,_and_early_career">Early life, education, and early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life, education, and early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eunice Mary Kennedy was born in <a href="/wiki/Brookline,_Massachusetts" title="Brookline, Massachusetts">Brookline, Massachusetts</a> on July 10, 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> She was the fifth of nine children of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.">Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rose_Kennedy" title="Rose Kennedy">Rose Fitzgerald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnndeath_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnndeath-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Her siblings included U.S. President John F. Kennedy, U.S. Attorney General and U.S. Senator Robert F. Kennedy, U.S. Senator Ted Kennedy, and U.S. Ambassador to Ireland Jean Kennedy Smith.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Shriver was educated at the Convent of The Sacred Heart, Roehampton, London and at <a href="/wiki/Manhattanville_College" title="Manhattanville College">Manhattanville College</a> in Upper Manhattan. After graduating from <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a> degree in <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> in 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> she worked for the Special War Problems Division of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a>. She eventually moved to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">U.S. Justice Department</a> as executive secretary for a project dealing with <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">juvenile delinquency</a>. She served as a <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social worker</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Alderson_Federal_Prison_Camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Alderson Federal Prison Camp">Federal Industrial Institution for Women</a> for one year before moving to <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> in 1951 to work with the <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Good_Shepherd" title="House of the Good Shepherd">House of the Good Shepherd</a> <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_shelter" title="Women&#39;s shelter">women's shelter</a> and the Chicago Juvenile Court.<sup id="cite_ref-baranauckas_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baranauckas-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work_and_awards">Charity work and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Charity work and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom_recipients" title="List of Presidential Medal of Freedom recipients">List of Presidential Medal of Freedom recipients</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg/300px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg/450px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg/600px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2936" data-file-height="1872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_in_1980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eunice Kennedy Shriver in 1980</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg/220px-US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg/330px-US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg/440px-US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="277" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US-NIH-NICHD-2008Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Child_Health_and_Human_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Child Health and Human Development">National Institute of Child Health and Human Development</a> was renamed in honor of Eunice Kennedy Shriver.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Shriver.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kennedy_Shriver.jpg/220px-Kennedy_Shriver.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kennedy_Shriver.jpg/330px-Kennedy_Shriver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kennedy_Shriver.jpg/440px-Kennedy_Shriver.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_Shriver.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eunice Kennedy Shriver speaks at March 3, 2008 ceremony in her honor</div></div></div>
<p>Shriver became executive vice president of the <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Jr._Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Jr. Foundation">Joseph P. Kennedy, Jr. Foundation</a> in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> She shifted the organization's focus from Catholic charities to research on the causes of intellectual disabilities and humane ways to treat them.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This interest eventually culminated in, among other things, the Special Olympics movement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>A longtime advocate for children's health and disability issues, Shriver championed the creation of the President's Panel on Mental Retardation in 1961. The panel was significant in the movement from institutionalization to <a href="/wiki/Community_integration" title="Community integration">community integration</a> in the US and throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Shriver was a key founder of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Child_Health_and_Human_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Child Health and Human Development">National Institute of Child Health and Human Development</a> (NICHD), a part of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> in 1962. She has also helped to establish numerous other university programs, government initiatives, health-care facilities, and support service networks throughout the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1962, Shriver founded Camp Shriver, a camp for children with special needs that was held on her Maryland farm. Camp Shriver and later evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Shriver founded the Special Olympics in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> That year, the Joseph P. Kennedy Jr. Foundation helped to plan and fund the First International Special Olympics Summer Games, held in Chicago, Illinois. In her speech at the opening ceremony, Shriver said, "'The Chicago Special Olympics prove a very fundamental fact, the fact that exceptional children — children with mental retardation — can be exceptional athletes, the fact that through sports they can realize their potential for growth.'" Special Olympics Inc. was established as a nonprofit charity in 1968; since that time, nearly three million athletes have participated.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1969, Shriver moved to France and pursued her interest in intellectual disability there. She started organizing small activities with Paris organizations, mostly reaching out to families of kids who had special needs to provide activities for them, laying the foundation for a robust international expansion of the Special Olympics in the late 1970s and 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-ABILITY_Magazine_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABILITY_Magazine-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1982, Shriver founded the Eunice Kennedy Shriver National Center for Community of Caring at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah" title="University of Utah">University of Utah, Salt Lake City</a>. The Community is a "<a href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="K–12 (education)">grades K-12</a>, whole school, comprehensive character education program with a focus on disabilities... adopted by almost 1,200 schools nationwide and in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Shriver was awarded the nation's highest civilian award, the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, in 1984 by U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a><sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> for her work on behalf of persons with disabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1990 Shriver was awarded the Eagle Award from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Sports_Academy" title="United States Sports Academy">United States Sports Academy</a>. The Eagle Award is the Academy's highest international honor and was awarded to Shriver for her significant contributions to international sport.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1992, Shriver received the Award for Greatest Public Service Benefiting the Disadvantaged, an award given out annually by <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service" title="Jefferson Awards for Public Service">Jefferson Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>For her work in nationalizing the Special Olympics, Shriver received the <a href="/wiki/Civitan_International" title="Civitan International">Civitan International</a> World Citizenship Award.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Her advocacy on this issue has also earned her other awards and recognitions, including honorary degrees from numerous universities.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-specialbio_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-specialbio-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> She is the second American and only woman to appear on a US coin while still living. Her portrait is on the obverse of the 1995 commemorative silver dollar honoring the Special Olympics. On the reverse is the quotation, "As we hope for the best in them, hope is reborn in us."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1998, Shriver was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Women&#39;s Hall of Fame">National Women's Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Shriver received the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt_Award_(NCAA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodore Roosevelt Award (NCAA)">Theodore Roosevelt Award</a> (the Teddy),<sup id="cite_ref-ncaa_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncaa-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> an annual award given by the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> to a graduate from an NCAA member institution who earned a <a href="/wiki/Varsity_letter" title="Varsity letter">varsity letter</a> in college for participation in <a href="/wiki/College_athletics" title="College athletics">intercollegiate athletics</a>, and who ultimately became a distinguished citizen of national reputation based on outstanding life accomplishment.  In addition to the Teddy recognition, she was selected in 2006 as part of the NCAA Centennial celebration as one of the 100 most-influential individuals in its first century; she was listed ninth.<sup id="cite_ref-ncaa_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncaa-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, she received a <a href="/wiki/Papal_Orders_of_Chivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal Orders of Chivalry">papal knighthood</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>, being made a Dame of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St._Gregory_the_Great" title="Order of St. Gregory the Great">Order of St. Gregory the Great</a> (DSG).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Her mother had been created a <a href="/wiki/Papal_count" class="mw-redirect" title="Papal count">papal countess</a> in 1950 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, she received the Foremother Award from the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Health_Research" title="National Center for Health Research">National Center for Health Research</a> for her lifetime achievements.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a> changed the NICHD's name to the <i>Eunice Kennedy Shriver</i> National Institute of Child Health and Human Development.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  In December 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> named Shriver the first recipient of <a href="/wiki/Sportsman_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Sportsman of the Year">Sportsman of the Year</a> Legacy Award.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  On May 9, 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Portrait_Gallery_(United_States)" title="National Portrait Gallery (United States)">National Portrait Gallery</a> (NPG) in Washington, D.C., unveiled an historic portrait of her, the first portrait the NPG has ever commissioned of an individual who had not served as a U.S. President or <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a>. The portrait depicts her with four Special Olympics athletes (including <a href="/wiki/Loretta_Claiborne" title="Loretta Claiborne">Loretta Claiborne</a>) and one <a href="/wiki/Best_Buddies_International" title="Best Buddies International">Best Buddies</a> participant. It was painted by <a href="/wiki/David_Lenz" title="David Lenz">David Lenz</a>, the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Outwin_Boochever_Portrait_Competition" class="mw-redirect" title="Outwin Boochever Portrait Competition">Outwin Boochever Portrait Competition</a> in 2006. As part of the Portrait Competition prize, the NPG commissioned a work from the winning artist to depict a living subject for the collection. Lenz, whose son, Sam, has <a href="/wiki/Down_syndrome" title="Down syndrome">Down syndrome</a> and is an enthusiastic Special Olympics athlete, was inspired by Shriver's dedication to working with people with intellectual disabilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Shriver became involved with <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Hamill" title="Dorothy Hamill">Dorothy Hamill</a>'s special skating program in the Special Olympics after Hamill's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">ice-skating</a> win. In September 2010, the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Brockport" class="mw-redirect" title="State University of New York at Brockport">State University of New York at Brockport</a>, home of the 1979 Special Olympics, renamed its football stadium after Shriver.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, Shriver posthumously received the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe_Courage_Award" title="Arthur Ashe Courage Award">Arthur Ashe Courage Award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2017_ESPY_Awards" title="2017 ESPY Awards">2017</a> <a href="/wiki/ESPY_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPY Awards">ESPY Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_involvement">Political involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Shriver actively campaigned for her elder brother, John, during his successful <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">1960 U.S. presidential election</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 
</p><p>Although Shriver was a Democrat, she was a vocal supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Pro-life_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-life movement">pro-life movement</a>. In 1990, Shriver wrote a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> denouncing the misuse of a quotation by President Kennedy used out of context by a <a href="/wiki/Pro-choice" class="mw-redirect" title="Pro-choice">pro-choice</a> group.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> During <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill Clinton presidential campaign, 1992">1992 Democratic U.S. presidential campaign</a>, she was one of several prominent Democrats – including <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors of Pennsylvania">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_P._Casey" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert P. Casey">Robert P. Casey</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bishop_(Catholic_Church)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop (Catholic Church)">Bishop</a> <a href="/wiki/Austin_Vaughan" class="mw-redirect" title="Austin Vaughan">Austin Vaughan</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> – who signed a letter to <i>The New York Times</i> protesting the Democratic Party's pro-choice plank in its <a href="/wiki/Party_platform" title="Party platform">platform</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Shriver was a supporter of several pro-life organizations: <a href="/wiki/Feminists_for_Life" title="Feminists for Life">Feminists for Life of America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Susan_B._Anthony_List" title="Susan B. Anthony List">Susan B. Anthony List</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Democrats_for_Life_of_America" title="Democrats for Life of America">Democrats for Life of America</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>A lifelong <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a>, Shriver supported her <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Son-in-law" class="mw-redirect" title="Son-in-law">son-in-law</a> <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>'s successful <a href="/wiki/California_gubernatorial_recall_election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="California gubernatorial recall election, 2003">2003 Governor of California election</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On January 28, 2008, Shriver was present at <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, when her brother, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Edward M. Kennedy</a>, announced his endorsement of <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">2008 Democratic U.S. presidential campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg/220px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg/330px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg/440px-Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1014" data-file-height="994" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver_and_Sargent_Shriver.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eunice and Sargent Shriver in 1999</div></div></div>
<p>On May 23, 1953, Shriver married <a href="/wiki/Sargent_Shriver" title="Sargent Shriver">Sargent Shriver</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> ceremony at <a href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Cathedral,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Patrick&#39;s Cathedral, New York">Saint Patrick's Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JFKLibrary_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKLibrary-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Her husband served as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_France" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Ambassador to France">U.S. Ambassador to France</a> from 1968 to 1970 and was the 1972 Democratic U.S. Vice Presidential candidate (with <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a> as the candidate for <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-JFKLibrary_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKLibrary-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> They had five children: <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Shriver" title="Bobby Shriver">Robert Sargent Shriver III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Shriver" title="Maria Shriver">Maria Owings Shriver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Shriver" title="Timothy Shriver">Timothy Perry Shriver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Shriver" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Shriver">Mark Kennedy Shriver</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Shriver" title="Anthony Shriver">Anthony Paul Kennedy Shriver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Shriver had nineteen grandchildren, the second-most of any of her siblings (her brother <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert</a> had eleven children who have produced thirty-four grandchildren).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Her daughter Maria Shriver is divorced from actor and former <a href="/wiki/California_Governor" class="mw-redirect" title="California Governor">California Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Shriver had a close relationship with her sister, <a href="/wiki/Rosemary_Kennedy" title="Rosemary Kennedy">Rosemary Kennedy</a>, who was intellectually disabled and who became incapacitated due to a lobotomy.<sup id="cite_ref-baranauckas_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baranauckas-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shriver suffered a stroke and broken hip in 2005.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On November 18, 2007, she was admitted to <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Hospital" title="Massachusetts General Hospital">Massachusetts General Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, where she spent several weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-2007hospital_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007hospital-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 7, 2009, Shriver was admitted to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod_Hospital" title="Cape Cod Hospital">Cape Cod Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hyannis,_Massachusetts" title="Hyannis, Massachusetts">Hyannis, Massachusetts</a> with an undisclosed ailment.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>  On August 10, her relatives were called to the hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Shriver died at the hospital on August 11, 2009 at age 88.<sup id="cite_ref-cnndeath_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnndeath-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shriver's family issued a statement upon her death, reading in part:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Inspired by her love of God, her devotion to her family, and her relentless belief in the dignity and worth of every human life, she worked without ceasing—searching, pushing, demanding, hoping for change. She was a living prayer, a living advocate, a living center of power. She set out to change the world and to change us, and she did that and more. She founded the movement that became Special Olympics, the largest movement for acceptance and inclusion for people with intellectual disabilities in the history of the world. Her work transformed the lives of hundreds of millions of people across the globe, and they in turn are her living legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> remarked after Shriver's death that she was "an extraordinary woman who, as much as anyone, taught our nation—and our world—that no physical or mental barrier can restrain the power of the human spirit."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funeral_and_burial">Funeral and burial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Funeral and burial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 14, 2009, an invitation-only <a href="/wiki/Requiem_Mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Requiem Mass">Requiem Mass</a> was celebrated for Shriver at St. Francis Xavier Roman Catholic Church in Hyannis.  Following the Requiem Mass, she was buried at the St. Francis Xavier parish cemetery in nearby <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Massachusetts" title="Centerville, Massachusetts">Centerville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-turnto10_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turnto10-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Pope <a href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> sent a letter of condolence to her family.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Because her brother <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted</a> had <a href="/wiki/Terminal_illness" title="Terminal illness">terminal</a> <a href="/wiki/Brain_cancer" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain cancer">brain cancer</a>, he was unable to attend the funeral,<sup id="cite_ref-abcjean_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcjean-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and their sister Jean Smith stayed with him. Ted died two weeks later,<sup id="cite_ref-abcjean_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcjean-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> leaving Jean as the sole surviving child of Joseph and Rose Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
